<div id="review_2346832384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346832384" />
    <a title=" Sarah Lumos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66292681-sarah-lumos"><img alt=" Sarah Lumos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548279135p2/66292681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346832384?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Sarah Lumos" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Sarah Lumos" href="/user/show/66292681-sarah-lumos"> Sarah Lumos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=inspiring">inspiring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=philosophical">philosophical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=neuroscience">neuroscience</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=made-me-think-about-life">made-me-think-about-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=social-work">social-work</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=gave-me-the-feels">gave-me-the-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=health-recovery-and-healing">health-recovery-and-healing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66292681-sarah-lumos?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346832384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17399123105742475172">Ever since reading <i> “Still Alice” </i>, I have made it my mission to finish all of Lisa Genova’s novels. Reading her books is both a vicarious and intellectual experience. Albeit entertaining, the pathology of the neuropsychological conditions in her books are evidence-based. She combines her knowledge of neuroscience and writing to craft stories that make learning about neurological diseases accessible. <br/><br/>Sarah is a woman striving to have it all, and in many ways does. She has a graduate degree from </span>
  <span id="freeText17399123105742475172" style="display:none">Ever since reading <i> “Still Alice” </i>, I have made it my mission to finish all of Lisa Genova’s novels. Reading her books is both a vicarious and intellectual experience. Albeit entertaining, the pathology of the neuropsychological conditions in her books are evidence-based. She combines her knowledge of neuroscience and writing to craft stories that make learning about neurological diseases accessible. <br /><br />Sarah is a woman striving to have it all, and in many ways does. She has a graduate degree from Harvard Business School, a stellar job as a top executive at a consulting firm, and a loving family. However, when a car accident impacts the right hemisphere of her brain, everything takes a drastic turn. She develops <i> “Left Neglect” </i> , a neurological condition where the person is no longer aware they have a left side. People with hemispatial neglect are not blind, rather as Sarah describes it, <i> <b> “What I perceive, and what I understand to be true are at war inside my head, fighting to the death, giving me a colossal headache.” </b></i> <br /><br />More than anything, this made me realize that life is unpredictable; everything can change in a second. I, like many others, live a life of delayed gratification. My inner monologue is, <i> "Once I finish graduate school I will do this, once I get a job I will do that.”</i> Sometimes I get so wrapped up in the future, I forget to enjoy the day-to-day experiences of my life. <br /><br />It was a gratifying and enlightening to see Sarah change. As the novel progresses, she learns to reevaluate her priorities, slow down, reconnect with loved ones, and change her outlook. She realizes success is not a linear road: <i> <b> “And I’m starting to wonder. What else is there? Maybe success can be something else, and maybe there’s another way to get there. Maybe there’s a different road for me with a more reasonable speed limit. Whether it’s because I can’t, I’m not afraid, something inside me has changed and wants something different, or a complex blend of all three, I can’t say, but I don’t want to go back to Berkley. I don’t want to go back to that life." </b></i> <br /><br />I loved this book, but it lacked the punch <i> “Still Alice” </i> had. I wish this book dwelled further into the scientific aspect of hemispatial neglect. While Genova does a great job at highlighting the emotional impact of hemispatial neglect, I believe this book could have been enhanced if she spent more time explaining the pathophysiology of the disease. <br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed reading this novel and I look forward to reading further works by Genova. Although <i> “Left Neglected” </i> did not have the sophistication and emotional prowess of her debut novel, it helped me understand the emotional and physical impact hemispatial neglect can have on the survivor’s life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17399123105742475172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XpMJAaEZQNbPY8M22GYojGIvUHkLwrrzRZi8r/NJHrS9bBl6+8geRPc+gQj0TtCBUs8FlgI+R42/PqNEbaUxyg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BjhUBk8QK33EIJB+YuyKUaA4mU0zTH7JtabZzVjyW/7lx0R9FcF17/x90kBOxHJckNjMojqwg7dPAMYmxh50gA==')})
  }

Some escaped the deportation and were able to retreat into the wilderness. Others found their way back to Acadie. But many were exiled to Britain, France, or the future United States, where they faced suspicion and prejudice and struggled to settle into new lives.\n\nA unique biographical approach to the history <span id="freeTextContainer7634577309601510857">Lisa Genova graduated valedictorian, summa cum laude from Bates College with a degree in Biopsychology and has a Ph.D. in Neuroscience from Harvard University.<br/>​<br/>Acclaimed as the Oliver Sacks of fiction and the Michael Crichton of brain science, Lisa has captured a special place in contemporary fiction, writing stories that are equally inspired by neuroscience and the human spirit. She is the New Yo</span>
  <span id="freeText7634577309601510857" style="display:none">Lisa Genova graduated valedictorian, summa cum laude from Bates College with a degree in Biopsychology and has a Ph.D. in Neuroscience from Harvard University.<br />​<br />Acclaimed as the Oliver Sacks of fiction and the Michael Crichton of brain science, Lisa has captured a special place in contemporary fiction, writing stories that are equally inspired by neuroscience and the human spirit. She is the New York Times bestselling author of STILL ALICE, LEFT NEGLECTED, LOVE ANTHONY, INSIDE THE O'BRIENS, and EVERY NOTE PLAYED.<br /><br />Her first nonfiction book, REMEMBER: The Science of Memory &amp; the Art of Forgetting, will be released March 23, 2021.<br />​<br />STILL ALICE was adapted into a film starring Julianne Moore, Alec Baldwin, Kristen Stewart, Kate Bosworth and Hunter Parrish. Julianne Moore won the 2015 Best Actress Oscar for her role as Alice Howland.<br /><br />EVERY NOTE PLAYED is being adapted into a film starring Angelina Jolie and Christoph Waltz, directed by Michael Sucsy.<br /><br />The film adaption for INSIDE THE O'BRIENS is in production.<br />​<br />In 2015, Lisa was named one of the U.S. Top 50 Influencers in Aging. She has appeared on Dr. Oz, the TODAY show, CNN, PBS Newshour, NPR, and several documentary films. <br /><br />Her TED Talk, "What You Can Do To Prevent Alzheimer's" has been viewed over five million times. <br /> <br />She received The Pell Center Prize for Story in the Public Square, for "distinguished storytelling that has enriched the public dialogue," The Sargent and Eunice Shriver Profiles in Dignity Award, The Global Genes RARE Champions of Hope Award, and The American College of Neuropsychopharmacology Media Award for "informing the public about Treatment and ongoing research in medical illness."<br /><br />In 2016, she received an Honorary Doctorate of Humane Letters from Bates College, The Alzheimer's Association's Rita Hayworth Award, and The Huntington’s Disease Society of America Community Awareness Award. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.lisagenova.com">www.lisagenova.com</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.Facebook.com/authorlisagenova">www.Facebook.com/authorlisagenova</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.Instagram.com/authorlisagenova">www.Instagram.com/authorlisagenova</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7634577309601510857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
